By January 31, 2025, Grafana migrated any remaining API Keys to Service Account Tokens (SATs) automatically and removed the API key endpoints.\n\n## Authentication Methods\n\nHTTP API requests can be authenticated using basic authentication, a service account token, or a session cookie.\n\n## API Key Scope and Validation\n\nAPI keys specify a role—either Admin, Editor, or Viewer—that determine the permissions associated with interacting with Grafana. The secondsToLive parameter sets the amount of time before the key expires, and it must be 2592000 (30 days) or less.\n\n## Service Accounts (Replacement)\n\nAPI keys are deprecated, and service accounts now replace API keys for authenticating with the HTTP APIs and interacting with Grafana. Compared to API keys, service accounts have limited scopes that provide more security.\n\nWhen migrating, desired scopes and expiration date are specified when creating the service account. By default, service account tokens don't have an expiration date, but if token_expiration_day_limit is set to a value greater than 0, Grafana restricts the lifetime limit of new tokens to the configured value in days.\n\n## Best Practices\n\nIt is strongly recommended to set the key's time to live for a shorter time, such as a few hours or less, creating much less risk than having API keys that are valid for a long time.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01LjFq2gghqsUvqq7p5Lh9dY","session_id":"a96ab398-c9e4-4171-9186-4d793587f707","uuid":"bc6443b1-aff1-4ff7-bfc4-6287f3239c01"}

\"path\": \"pkg/services/authn/clients/api_key.go\",\n      \"symbol\": \"validateApiKey\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"Grafana implements API key authentication through a multi-layered architecture combining authentication clients, service layers, and database operations.\\n\\n**Authentication Flow:**\\nThe primary authentication flow starts at `pkg/services/contexthandler/contexthandler.go:Middleware()`, which sets up the request context and invokes the authenticator. The `pkg/services/authn/authnimpl/service.go:Service.Authenticate()` method orchestrates the authentication process by iterating through registered clients in priority order. For API keys, the `pkg/services/authn/clients/api_key.go:APIKey` client is registered with priority 30 and handles API key validation.\\n\\n**API Key Validation:**\\nThe `APIKey` client in `pkg/services/authn/clients/api_key.go` implements the `Authenticate()` method which:\\n1. Extracts the token from the Authorization header (Bearer prefix or basic auth with username='api_key')\\n2. Distinguishes between modern service account tokens (glXX_ prefix) and legacy API keys\\n3. Decodes the token using either `pkg/components/satokengen/tokengen.go:Decode()` for modern tokens or `pkg/components/apikeygen/apikeygen.go` for legacy keys\\n4. Retrieves the API key from the database via `pkg/services/apikey/apikeyimpl/xorm_store.go:GetAPIKeyByHash()` or `GetApiKeyByName()`\\n5. Validates the key using `validateApiKey()` which checks:\\n   - Expiration status (comparing `expires` timestamp with current time)\\n   - Revocation status (checking `is_revoked` flag)\\n   - Organization membership (verifying `org_id` matches request)\\n   - Service account association (requiring `service_account_id` to be set)\\n\\n**Expiration Handling:**\\nAPI key expiration is enforced in `validateApiKey()` at line 213 of `pkg/services/authn/clients/api_key.go`: the `Expires` field (stored as Unix timestamp in int64) is compared against the current time. Expired keys return `errAPIKeyExpired`. The expiration time is set during key creation in `pkg/services/apikey/apikeyimpl/xorm_store.go:AddAPIKey()` using the `SecondsToLive` parameter to calculate the expiry Unix timestamp.\\n\\n**Scope Enforcement:**\\nScopes are enforced through the role-based access control system. API keys are associated with service accounts through the `ServiceAccountId` field in `pkg/services/apikey/model.go:APIKey`.
